<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001008"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>HAPPY, LUMINOUS AND FRUITFUL YEAR 2004 !<br />
Prosveta Publishing is pleased to offer you the Daily Meditation for this 2004-01-15.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
"If you are insignificant and little known in society, you are powerless to intervene in the affairs of state. To be able to do so, you must go all the way to the centre (or to the summit, which is symbolically the same) where the king or president is to be found, and become his minister. At that moment, yes, you have every possibility, because you have reached the central point, or the zenith. As long as you remain below, or on the periphery, no-one listens to you. And the same law applies in the spiritual realm. As long as you do not succeed in reaching the centre or the summit within you, that is to say your spirit, you can achieve certain things, of course, but you are not truly in charge of anything. Whereas once you manage to link with your spirit, you are the master, because this centre affords you all possibilities, and you are fully in charge. So, stop being concerned with achievements that are futile and transitory; work to reach the spirit within you, without worrying about the time it will take."<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
Omraam Mikhaël Aïvanhov<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001008.html">03:43 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1008" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001103"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p><a href="http://www.baseboard.net/forums/showthread.php?s=f6650e45b2e36239105377b004b0e244&postid=140181#post140181">Apple Boot Key Combos</a></p>

<p><br />
Bypass startup drive and boot from external (or CD)....CMD-OPT-SHIFT-DELETE<br />
Boot from CD (Most late model Apples) ................. C<br />
Boot from a specific SCSI ID #.(#=SCSI ID number)...... CMD-OPT-SHIFT-DELETE-#<br />
Zap PRAM .............................................. CMD-OPT-P-R<br />
Disable Extensions .................................... SHIFT<br />
Rebuild Desktop ....................................... CMD-OPT<br />
Close finder windows.(hold just before finder starts).. OPT<br />
Boot with Virtual Memory off........................... CMD<br />
Trigger extension manager at boot-up................... SPACE<br />
Force Quadra av machines to use TV as a monitor........ CMD-OPT-T-V<br />
Boot from ROM (Mac Classic only)....................... CMD-OPT-X-O<br />
Force PowerBooks to reset the screen................... R<br />
Force an AV monitor to be recognized as one............ CMD-OPT-A-V<br />
Eject Boot Floppy...................................... Hold Down Mouse Button<br />
Select volume to start from............................ OPT<br />
Start in Firewire drive mode........................... T<br />
Startup in OSX if OS9 and OXS in boot partition........ X or CMD-X<br />
Hold down until the 2nd chime, will boot into 9?....... CMD-OPT<br />
OSX: Watch the status of the system load............... CMD-V<br />
OSX: Enter single-user mode (shell-level mode)......... CMD-S<br />
_<br />
After startup:</p>

<p>Bring up dialogue for shutdown/sleep/restart........... POWER<br />
Eject a Floppy Disk.................................... CMD-SHIFT-1 or(2) or (0)<br />
Force current app to quit.............................. CMD-OPT-ESC<br />
Unconditionally reboot................................. CTRL-CMD-POWER<br />
Fast Shutdown.......................................... CTRL-CMD-OPT-POWER<br />
Goto the debugger (if MacsBug is installed)............ CMD-POWER<br />
Reset Power Manager on PowerBooks...................... USE THIS LINK <br />
Put late model PowerBooks & Desktops to sleep.......... CMD-OPT-POWER<br />
_</p>

<p>Application Specific Keys:</p>

<p>Startup key combos to reset the resolution on video boards:<br />
SuperMac (at least some models)press&hold.............. OPT<br />
Imagine 128 Card (reset resolution).................... N<br />
RasterOps (at least some models)press&hold............. CMD-OPT-SHIFT<br />
Radius (Use cable sense pins to set resolution)........ U<br />
Radius (Cycle through available resolutions)........... T<br />
_<br />
Conflict Catcher:<br />
Pause Boot........................................... P<br />
Launch CC at Startup................................. SPACE or CAPS LOCK<br />
Skip remaining extensions............................ CMD-PERIOD<br />
Reboot cleanly while loading extensions.............. CMD-R<br />
_<br />
RAM Doubler:<br />
Disable at Startup................................... ~ (Tilde) or ESC<br />
_<br />
Apple System Installer:<br />
Change custom install to clean install............... CMD-Shift-K<br />
_<br />
Claris Emailer:<br />
Bypass specified startup connections................. Hold CMD at launch<br />
Bring up rebuild options............................. Hold OPT at launch</p>

<p>Controlling the Post-Startup Environment</p>

<p>Most Macintosh users know about holding the Shift key down to prevent extensions from loading, but there are numerous startup modifiers that affect the state of the system after the boot process finishes.</p>

<p>* Shift causes the Mac to boot without extensions, which is useful for troubleshooting extension conflicts. If you hold down Shift after all the extensions have loaded but before the Finder launches, it also prevents any startup items from launching.</p>

<p>* Spacebar launches Apple's Extensions Manager early in the startup process so you can enable or disable extensions before they load. Casady & Greene's Conflict Catcher, if you're using it instead of Extensions Manager, also launches if it sees you holding down the spacebar, or, optionally, if Caps Lock is activated. Conflict Catcher also adds the capability to configure additional startup keys as ways of specifying that a particular startup set should be used. Choose Edit Sets from the Sets menu, select a set in the resulting dialog and click Modify. In the sub-dialog that appears, you can specify a startup key and check the checkbox to make it effective.</p>

<p>* Option, if held down as the Finder launches, closes any previously open Finder windows. On stock older Macs, holding down Option does nothing at startup by default, although some extensions may deactivate if Option is held down when they attempt to load; see below for Option's effect on new Macs and Macs with Zip drives.</p>

<p>* Control can cause the Location Manager to prompt you to select a location. Although Control is the default, you can redefine it in the Location Manager's Preferences dialog, and since Control held down at startup also activates Apple's MacsBug debugger (see below), you may wish to pick a different key combination.</p>

<p>* Command turns virtual memory off until the next restart.</p>

<p>* Shift-Option disables extensions other than Connectix's RAM Doubler (and MacsBug - see below). To disable RAM Doubler but no other extensions, hold down the tilde (~) key at startup.</p>

<p>Choosing Startup Disks</p>

<p>Not surprisingly, many of the startup modifiers affect the disk used to boot the Mac. A number of these are specific to certain models of the Macintosh.</p>

<p>* The mouse button causes the Mac to eject floppy disks and most other forms of removable media, though not CD-ROMs. *?*</p>

<p>* The C key forces the Mac to start up from a bootable CD-ROM, if one is present, which is useful if something goes wrong with your startup hard disk. This key doesn't work with some older Macs or clones that didn't use Apple CD-ROM drives; they require Command- Shift-Option-Delete instead (see below).</p>

<p>* Option activates the new Startup Manager on the iBook, Power Mac G4 (AGP Graphics), PowerBook (FireWire), and slot-loading iMacs. The Startup Manager displays a rather cryptic set of icons indicating available startup volumes, including any NetBoot volumes that are available. On some Macs with Iomega Zip drives, holding down Option at startup when there is a Zip startup disk inserted will cause the Mac to boot from the Zip disk.</p>

<p>* Command-Shift-Option-Delete bypasses the disk selected in the Startup Disk control panel in favor of an external device or from CD-ROM (on older Macs). This is also useful if your main hard disk is having problems and you need to start up from another device. (On some PowerBooks, however, this key combination merely ignores the internal drive, which isn't as useful.)</p>

<p>* The D key forces the PowerBook (Bronze Keyboard and FireWire) to boot from the internal hard disk.</p>

<p>* The T key forces the PowerBook (FireWire) (and reportedly the Power Mac G4 (AGP Graphics), though I was unable to verify that on my machine) to start up in FireWire Target Disk Mode, which is essentially the modern equivalent of SCSI Disk Mode and enables a PowerBook (FireWire) to act as a FireWire-accessible hard disk for another Macintosh.</p>

<p><br />
Seriously Tweaky Startup Modifiers</p>

<p>Only programmers and the most geeky of users will find these startup modifiers useful.</p>

<p>* Control activates Apple's MacsBug debugger as soon as it loads. If you rely on this frequently, you may want to redefine the default key for selecting the Location Manager location at startup from Control to something else.</p>

<p>* Shift-Option disables extensions and virtual memory but still loads MacsBug, which would otherwise be disabled by the Shift key.</p>

<p>* Command-Option-O-F puts you into Open Firmware mode on PCI-based Macs and clones. Open Firmware is a cross-platform firmware standard for controlling hardware that all PCI-based Macs use. It's mostly of interest to hardware developers, but it can be a fun way to freak out a new user who's not expecting to see a command line on the Mac. To exit Open Firmware and continue booting, type "mac-boot" or "bye" (depending on Macintosh model) and press Return. For a list of commands you can enter while in Open Firmware mode, see the Tech Info Library article.</p>

<p>Just for Fun</p>

<p>Although Apple has moved away from relatively frivolous "Easter Eggs" connected with startup modifiers, there are a few available for old Macintosh models.</p>

<p>* Command-X-O, when held down at startup on a Macintosh Classic boots the Classic from a built-in ROM disk.</p>

<p>* Command-Option-C-I, when held down at startup on a Macintosh IIci whose date has been set to 20-Sep-89 (the machine's introduction date), produces some sort of graphical display that I can't check for lack of a relevant machine. A different display appears if you hold down Command-Option-F-X at startup on a Macintosh IIfx with the date set to 19-Mar-90.</p>

<p>Jim A. Creak</p>

<h3 class="title">new to google: Mind Reading</h3>

but like different, eh?  </p>

as a replacement.</p>

<p>Just downt he page <a href="http://www.sgtclog.nl/">this</a> link for me.</p>

<p>                     so <br />
             trippy.</p>

<p><br />
     dear me.</p>

<p>google is<br />
reading me<br />
mind.</p>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001166"></a>
<h3 class="title">wow google rocks</h3>

<p>ok, on the phone to do some banklijk stuff in Canada and she needed the three letter abbreviation for the Netherlands (my current place of domicile)</p>

<p><hr></p>

<p>"Three?"</p>

<p>"Umm, let me check google"</p>

<p>"Umm, EUR (Euro) or maybe NLG (Netherlands Guilder)?"</p>

<p><i>"No, sorry sir"</i></p>

<p>"How about NLD"</p>

<p><i>"NLD?"</i></p>

<p><i>"That just might be it"</i></p>

<p><i>"The system seems to be accepting it"</i></p>

<p>"Yes."</p>

<p>"That was google"</p>

<p><i>"Is there anything else I can help you with today?"</i></p>

<p>"No.  Thank you very much."</p>

<p><i>"Have an excellent day."</i></p>

<p>"Have a great day!"</p>

<p><br />
<hr></p>

<p>Wow.</p>

	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001166.html">09:27 pm</a>

<h2 class="date">april 26, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001162"></a>
<h3 class="title">last one for today</h3>

<p>scariest yet.  everything I learned today in one shiny package.</p>

<pre>
find . -name '*arp_warp.log' -cmin -30 -exec sh -c "grep 'Building Cycle' /dev/null {} | tail -1" \;
</pre>




<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001162.html">07:41 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1162" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001161"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>Thank you <a href="http://www.ccs.uky.edu/~mahesh/unixtips.html">Unix Guru List</a>.  You rocked my world by showing me how to do multiple commands in a find command:</p>

<p>Their's:</p>

<pre>
find . -xdev -type d -exec /bin/echo -n {} \; -exec sh -c "ls {} | wc -l" \;
</pre>

<p>But, really, stripped down to it's basics, to run multiple commands, it's:</p>

<pre>
find . -exec sh -c "ls {} | wc -l" \;
</pre>

<p>Sweetness.  Find running multiple commands in a pipe-d exec.  This does a neat trick, it runs "sh" (the Bourne Shell (probably the bash shell on your box)) with the -c argument, meaning, take the next string as the script to execute.</p>

<p>Ok, now I can take over the world.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001161.html">05:45 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1161" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001160"></a>
<h3 class="title">find rocks.</h3>

<p>OK, my killer find command of the day.  Oh yeah, "alias c clear".</p>

<pre>
c ; find . -name '*_arp_warp.log' -cmin -10 -exec sh -c 'grep "Building Cycle" {} | tail -1' \;
</pre>

<p>Cool.</p>

<p>This one looks through a CCP4i directory for running arp_warp jobs and tells you what cycle each one is in.  Add a "-print" or "-printf" (before the -exec) for more fun.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001160.html">05:36 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1160" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001142"></a>
<h3 class="title">sweet.</h3>

<p><a href="http://www.dwdrums.com/pedals/9000Pedals.htm"><br />
<img alt="9000-Pedals.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/9000-Pedals.jpg" width="750" height="377" border="0" /><br />
DW 9002 Double Bass Drum Pedal</a><br />
I always wanted Drum Workshop pedals, so bad.  But way too expensive and I didn't like the upraised logo on the pedal, hard on the voeten. </p>

<p>However, since I'm going all out here on the <b>ultimate sness drum set</b>, why not.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001142.html">09:07 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1142" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001141"></a>
<h3 class="title">roland spd-11 - main drum unit</h3>

<p><a href="http://www.sonicstate.com/synth/roland_spd-11.cfm"><br />
<img alt="roland_spd-11.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/roland_spd-11.jpg" width="400" height="315" border="0" /><br />
Roland SPD-11</a></p>

<p>I have this one.  I bought it back in 1999.  Very sweet.  Still a little loud for an apartment though.  Within a proper drumset, it would play a critical and fun part.  I see it as providing all the bass drum sounds, as well as all the tomtom sounds, special effects and MIDI control.</p>

<p>For the bass drum, I know, I know, an acoustic one is nice.  But, but with the spd-11 hooked up to a good subwoofer, you can get some killer bass drum sounds, and a wide variety of kinds of bass drum sounds.  Way better than a big huge, hard to transport drum capable of just making one sound.</p>

<p>In a drumming utopia, I'd have both electronic and acoustic. </p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001141.html">09:01 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1141" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001136"></a>
<h3 class="title">43-m1x</h3>

<p><br />
<h3>Re-Mix Crash</h3><br />
<img alt="fx_remixcrash.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/fx_remixcrash.jpg" width="144" height="107" border="0" /></p>

<p>A colorful, short, fast crash. A rich musical sound that is all "crash" with almost no sustain. Concentrated sound that speaks and then cuts out immediately. Full-bodied and quite powerful for it's size. Very versatile.<br />
 </p>

<p>     <br />
 <br />
Played by<br />
 <br />
Terri Lyne Carrington<br />
Zach Danziger<br />
Victor Loyo<br />
 <br />
   <br />
 </p>

<p><h3>Re-Mix Breakbeat Ride</h3><br />
<img alt="fx_remixbreakbeatride.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/fx_remixbreakbeatride.jpg" width="144" height="107" border="0" /><br />
An alarmingly faithful acoustic recreation of the ride beat sound heard on the most common "breakbeat" loops. Joins the existing Re-Mix range now giving the "Techno" player the full spectrum of cymbal sounds for modern electronically influenced music.  <br />
 <br />
</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001136.html">08:30 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1136" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001135"></a>
<h3 class="title">crash of doom</h3>

<p><a href="http://www.zildjian.com/product.asp?se=6&ty=C&ID=70#"><br />
<img alt="fx_crashofdoom.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/fx_crashofdoom.jpg" width="144" height="107" border="0" /><br />
Oriental Crash of Doom</a><br />
A truly one of a kind monster Crash. Ultra-trashy, very dark and low pitched. Features an immediate, explosive attack and a tremendous, broad, full-bodied sustain. An exceptionally exotic sound for special accents and effects. The 18" is higher-pitched, but equally trashy.<br />
</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001135.html">08:25 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1135" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>

<h2 class="date">april 18, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">

<h3 class="title">Nanognomes of Zurich</h3>

<table>
<tr>
<td>
<a href="http://www.zurich.ibm.com/st/storage/millipede.html">
<img alt="single_366.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/single_366.jpg" width="366" height="278" border="0" />
</td>
<td>
<img alt="array_375.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/array_375.jpg" width="375" height="279" border="0" />
</td>
</tr>
</table>

<p><a href="http://www.zurich.ibm.com/st/storage/millipede.html">millipede</a> - With data densities in the hundreds of Gb/in² range, these are the <i><b>nano-punchcards</b></i>, so cool.  </p>

<p>From <a href="http://www.zurich.ibm.com">(IBM) Zurich</a>.  So you know, <a href="http://www.ifi.unizh.ch/CL/rinaldi/gnomes.html">the gnomes</a>.</p>

<p>Thanks <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk">BBC International</a>, but off of AM radio.  Cool.<br />
</p>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001120"></a>
<h3 class="title">Julia Butterfly Hill - Tree dancer</h3>

<p>From the <a href="http://www.mailermailer.com/x?oid=17943f">Circle of Life mailing list</a>:</p>

<p><i class="julia"><br />
Julia's 30 Candles</p>

<p>Thoughts From Julia Butterfly Hill<br />
My 30th Birthday<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
I'm turning 30. Gasp! "How does it feel?" everyone asks. I laugh. It feels like another day to me. I almost feel badly for my blasé response--as if I should be apologizing or something. But the reality is, I don't know if I have ever felt age appropriate. When I was little, I grew old really quickly; and now that I am getting older and have had more than one close brush with death, I feel like I am growing younger in many respects.</p>

<p>I've never fit very well into the roles expected of me. Of course these days, I don't know if anyone knows what to expect--least of all me.</p>

<p>I am full to overflowing with possibilities. I have 101 projects I want to do, and it is taking much of my time just doing the feasibility research for them. And because I am such a "doer," I am always chomping at the bit, ready to break into a full-fledged gallop even when I know I should steady the pace. This is a lifetime marathon after all, not a sprint.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
So I guess, if anything, I am just going through yet another gawky teenager stage; only this time I am going through it as I make the leap from my 20s into my 30s. So I proclaim it proudly--with no asterisks, no sidebar notations, and absolutely no idea what it actually means--"I am 30 years old!" It seems I know a heck of a lot about what 30 is not; and if anything, my gift to myself is the unknown excitement of discovering what 30 is--at least for me.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
So here's to another solar rotation, a monarch butterfly's winged migration, a bus powered by veggie oil in motion, a reclaiming democracy mobilization, and a reinvigorated, revolutionary Love-resolution.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
Lots of love and laughter, julia b<br />
</i>                                                                                                                        </p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001120.html">09:59 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1120" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001230"></a>
<h3 class="title">Rush : Rivendell</h3>

<p>Sunlight dances through the leaves<br />
Soft winds stir the sighing trees<br />
Lying in the warm grass<br />
Feel the sun upon your face<br />
Elven songs and endless nights<br />
Sweet wine and soft relaxing lights<br />
Time will never touch you<br />
Here in this enchanted place<br />
Chorus<br />
You feel there's something calling you<br />
You're wanting to return<br />
To where the misty mountains rise and friendly fires burn<br />
A place you can escape the world<br />
Where the dark lord cannot go<br />
Peace of mind and sanctuary by loud water's flow<br />
I've traveled now for many miles<br />
It feels so good to see the smiles of<br />
Friends who never left your mind<br />
When you were far away<br />
From the golden light of coming dawn<br />
Till the twilight where the sun is gone<br />
We treasure every season<br />
And every passing day<br />
We feel the coming of a new day<br />
Dark gives way to light a new way<br />
Stop here for a while until the world,<br />
The world calls you away<br />
Yet you know I've had the feeling<br />
Standing with my senses reeling<br />
This is the place to grow old 'til<br />
I reach my final day.<br />
Chorus<br />
 <br />
</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001230.html">10:20 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1230" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

by radish (98371)  on Friday May 14, @10:55AM (#9153982) <br />
(http://slashdot.org/)  <br />
Whereas the Linux one would come with a choice of saddles, none of which are<br />
particularly comfortable, and your choice of exactly 1 or 3 hand grips. You'd<br />
have to buy brakes, gears and chains seperatly, and a lot of the most popular<br />
ones wouldn't fit. Some models (made by Gentoobluar Bikes, inc) would<br />
actually just come as a big box of iron ore and a sheet of instructions. <br />
In german. <br />
</pre></p>

<h2 class="date">mei 14, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001227"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>using <a href="http://www-106.ibm.com/developerworks/linux/library/l-shared.html?ca=dgr-lnxw06ShareLinux">shared memory</a> in C++ on Linux.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001227.html">02:01 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1227" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001226"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>why <a href="http://www.onlamp.com/pub/a/onlamp/2004/05/06/writegreatcode.html">learning assembly</a> is still a <a href="http://info.astrian.net/jargon/terms/g/Good_Thing.html">good thing</a>.</p>

<p>and on the other side <a href="http://www.osnews.com/story.php?news_id=7038">scripting languages</a>. </p>

<p>I think they all have a place, assembly rocks for speed, C is fast and good, C++ is great for bigger projects, Tcl is great for quick scripts that might need GUI's, Perl is awesome for regexps, Python is good for quickly building applications, and has good integration with C, FORTRAN has great math libraries.</p>

<p>In my latest project, I've had to code in C, C++, Bourne shell, Python, Tcl and FORTRAN.  Tcl was the most fun.  C made me feel the best about myself.  FORTRAN was painful.  With Bourne shell, I was amazed at how much I could do.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001226.html">12:22 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1226" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

<h2 class="date">mei 12, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001220"></a>
<h3 class="title">trees</h3>

<p>Some types of tree datastructures</p>

<ol>
<li><a href="http://searchdatabase.techtarget.com/sDefinition/0,,sid13_gci509290,00.html">binary-tree</a>
A binary tree is a method of placing and locating files (called records or keys) in a database, especially when all the data is known to be in random access memory (RAM). The algorithm finds data by repeatedly dividing the number of ultimately accessible records in half until only one remains.
<img alt="binarytree.gif" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/binarytree.gif" width="178" height="217" border="0" />
</li>

<p><li><a href="http://searchdatabase.techtarget.com/sDefinition/0,,sid13_gci509290,00.html">B-tree</a><br />
A B-tree is a method of placing and locating files (called records or keys) in a database. (The meaning of the letter B has not been explicitly defined.). The maximum number of children per node is the order of the tree. The number of required disk accesses is the depth.<br />
<img alt="btree.gif" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/btree.gif" width="179" height="215" border="0" /><br />
</li></p>

<p><li><a href="http://searchdatabase.techtarget.com/sDefinition/0,,sid13_gci509290,00.html">quad tree</a><br />
A quad tree is a method of placing and locating files (called records or keys) in a database. The algorithm finds data by repeatedly dividing the number of ultimately accessible records in four parts until only one remains.<br />
<img alt="quad_tree.gif" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/quad_tree.gif" width="269" height="187" border="0" /><br />
</li></p>

<p><li><a href="http://searchdatabase.techtarget.com/sDefinition/0,,sid13_gci509290,00.html">splay tree</a><br />
A splay tree is a self-adjusting search algorithm for placing and locating files (called records or keys) in a database. The algorithm finds data by repeatedly making choices at decision points called nodes.<br />
</li></p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001220.html">01:39 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1220" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001210"></a>
<h3 class="title">things i spend my time thinking about.  by sness.  part 1, volume 23.</h3>

<p><code><br />
<a href="http://www.nethack.org"><b>Nethack</b></a>:<br />
Mom class<br />
---------<br />
Starting Inventory:</p>

<p>+2 rustproof knife<br />
+1 club (rolling pin)<br />
+0 alchemy smock<br />
+0 leather gloves<br />
+0 dented pot<br />
food: some pancakes, bananas, oranges, carrots, slime molds, a bit of<br />
garlic, a cream pie, candy bar, two random tins.<br />
2 potions of fruit juice<br />
1 ring: (normal ring generation rules)<br />
 50% gold<br />
 50% diamond<br />
a uncursed sack<br />
a tinning kit<br />
a tin opener<br />
5% spellbook of healing <br />
5% spellbook of cure sickness<br />
10% towel<br />
10% credit card<br />
10% camera</p>

<p><br />
Stats:</p>

<p>Str:  7-12<br />
Dex: 10-13<br />
Con: 10-15<br />
Int: 10-13<br />
Wis: 13-18<br />
Cha: 13-17</p>

<p><br />
Gained intrinsics:</p>

<p>XL1  food detection nose<br />
XL3  see invisible<br />
XL5  searching<br />
XL7  warning<br />
XL10 fire resistance<br />
XL12 cold resistance<br />
XL15 The Eye. (technique)</p>

<p><br />
Weapon / spell skills:</p>

<p>Unskilled - most stuff.<br />
Basic - short sword, mace, club, staff, unihorn (these are somewhat<br />
arbitrary), darts, bow (from summer camp as a little girl), barehanded<br />
combat, twoweapon (two knives prepare food *fast*), divination spells (can<br />
always find stuff), enchantment spells (cause fear, with "the look"...)<br />
Skilled - dagger, hammer (fixes stuff around the house), riding (summer<br />
camp), healing spells (she's not quite a doctor, but close.  SPECIAL<br />
SPELL: extra healing.)<br />
Expert - knife.</p>

<p>Quest:</p>

<p>guardian: Grandma.<br />
location: Back home.<br />
friendlies: sisters, maybe nephews and nieces, the old family cat.<br />
nemesis: purse snatcher<br />
other baddies: punk teenagers, possibly leprechauns, etc.  Also rats and<br />
   spiders and ants and other insects -- the sort of things that crawl around<br />
   in the alleyways where purse snatchers might hang out.</p>

<p>Quest Artifact:</p>

<p>Grandma's lucky purse: <br />
Bag of holding<br />
Intelligent<br />
Resists curses</p>

<p>wielded: damage of heavy iron ball<br />
carried: luckstone<br />
         +3 Cha if female<br />
         -3 Cha if male<br />
invoked: creates a random tool<br />
	 (excluding containers, magic lamps and bags of tricks)</p>

<p>Deities:</p>

<p>Lawful -  Susan B. Anthony<br />
Neutral - Indira Ghandi<br />
Chaotic - Martha Stewart</p>

<p>Techniques:</p>

<p>#prepare - prepare a corpse before eating it, adding some nutrition<br />
and flavor.  Takes 20 turns.<br />
</code></p>

<p>From an <a href="http://groups.google.com/groups?q=mom+class+nethack&hl=en&lr=&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&safe=off&selm=npx5b.164196%242x.46530%40rwcrnsc52.ops.asp.att.net&rnum=1">article</a> on google groups.  Well, there was this article, and this thread after it, and I extracted the tasty ideas from the thread and made some of their small suggested improvements. </p>

<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001202.html">10:38 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1202" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001201"></a>
<h3 class="title">exploring mars</h3>

<p><a href="http://marsrovers.jpl.nasa.gov/gallery/press/spirit/20040506a.html"><img alt="08-AK-01-traverse-map-B093R1_br.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/08-AK-01-traverse-map-B093R1_br.jpg" width="500" height="375" border="0" /></a><br />
This map illustrates the Mars Exploration Rover Spirit's position as of sol 112 (April 26, 2004), near the crater called "Missoula." Like a train on a tight schedule, Spirit will make regular stops along the way to its ultimate destination, the "Columbia Hills." At each stop, or "station," the rover will briefly analyze the area's rocks and soils. Each tick mark on the rover's route represents one sol's worth of travel, or about 60 to 70 meters (200 to 230 feet). Rover planners estimate that Spirit will reach the hills around mid-June. Presently, the rover is stopped at a site called "Plains Station." </p>

<p>The color thermal data show how well different surface features hold onto heat. Red indicates warmth; blue indicates coolness. Areas with higher temperatures are more likely to be rocky, as rocks absorb heat. Lower temperatures denote small particles and fewer rocks. During its traverse, Spirit will document the causes of these temperature variations. </p>

<p>The map comprises data from the camera on NASA's Mars Global Surveyor orbiter and the thermal emission imaging system on NASA's Mars Odyssey orbiter.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001201.html">09:44 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1201" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<p>both from <a href="http://www.bmsc.washington.edu/people/merritt/graphics/">Ethan Merritt's homepage</a></p>

	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001200.html">09:40 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1200" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001199"></a>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001197"></a>
<h3 class="title">pomes</h3>

<p>A poem for Manchester.</p>

<p>Vote for <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/manchester/arts/2004/05/05/poem1.shtml">this poem</a>.</p>

<p>Ok, not just yet, but <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/manchester/arts/2004/05/05/poem_update.shtml">soon!</a></p>

<p>And, the poem with proper formatting:</p>

<pre>
i came late, to manchester.
                                          
i circumambulated its music like hills, sweeping in on the smiths, an atlantic vulture, hungry for fog.
historically, i peaked over peeks from an unknown northern town.
now i search for my own industry
lost among the farms of didsbury.
                                                                                                                                                               
Karen Moore
</pre>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001197.html">08:51 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1197" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<a name="001186"></a>
<h3 class="title">Emacs is Fun</h3>

<p>Some Emacs Lisp packages for you nice kids:</p>

<ul>
<li><a href="http://www.nongnu.org/newsticker/">Newsticker</a> - A RSS aggregator</li>

<p><li><a href="http://nic-nac-project.de/~necui/AGONIA/page~highlight-tail.el/css~elisp">highlight-tail.el</a> - Show a highlighting tail of recently typed words</li></p>

<p><li><a href="http://www.vegetable.demon.co.uk/wence/multi-region.el">multi-region.el</a> - Apply commands to multiple regions at once</li></p>

<p><li><a href="http://www.ma.utexas.edu/~jcorneli/y/todl/">todl.el</a> - An enhanced TODO list for Emacs</li></p>

<p><li><a href="http://www.newartisans.com/johnw/Emacs/isearchb.el">isearchb.el</a> and <a href="http://www.newartisans.com/johnw/Emacs/iswitchb.el">iswitchb.el</a> - Makes switching buffers much easier</li></p>

<p></ul></p>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001184"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>As the man and the woman in me<br />
unite in love,<br />
the brilliant beauty<br />
balanced on the two-petalled lotus<br />
within me<br />
dazzles my eyes.<br />
The rays<br />
outshine the moon<br />
and the jewels<br />
glowing on the hoods of snakes.<br />
    <br />
My skin and bone<br />
are turned to gold.<br />
I am the reservoir of love<br />
alive as the waves.<br />
A single drop of water<br />
has grown into a sea,<br />
unnavigable.</p>

<p>-Lalan<br />
>From "Teachings of the Hindu Mystics," © 2001 by Andrew Harvey. Reprinted by arrangement with Shambhala Publications, Boston, www.shambhala.com.<br />
                                                                                                                                                               <br />
</p>

	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001184.html">09:39 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1184" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001177"></a>
<h3 class="title">awk rawks.</h3>

<p>Say you wanted to add 329 to the first column in a text file.  Well, one way to do it is with awk:</p>

<pre>
awk '{ printf "%f\t%f\t%f\n", $1+329, $2, $3  }' rms > rms-add
</pre>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001177.html">01:19 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1177" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001176"></a>
<h3 class="title">emacs w3 no color</h3>

<pre>
M-x w3
M-x set-variable w3-honor-stylesheets nil
C-o URL
</pre>

<p>Often, web pages have background colours set.  These often look good in a normal web browser, but "niet zo lekker" (not so tasty) in the Emacs web browser, <b>w3</b>.</p>

<p>To fix this, try the above commands.  These stop Emacs from using stylesheets, which is usually the place that people put color commands in, nowadays. </p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001176.html">12:10 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1176" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001170"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>LUNAR ECLIPSE: On May 4th, sky watchers in Europe, Africa and parts of Asia can see a total lunar eclipse. The full moon will glide through Earth's shadow and turn a lovely shade of sunset-red. The eclipse begins at 18:48 GMT (2:48 p.m. EDT) and becomes total at 19:52 GMT (3:52 p.m. EDT).</p>

<p>From <a href="http://www.spaceweather.com">spaceweather.com</a></p>

	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001170.html">08:13 am</a>

</div>



<h2 class="date">mei 02, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001169"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p><a href="http://erik.nerim.net/drop/language.htm">dropje</a></p>

<p>http://www.healthcentral.com/PeoplesPharmacy/PharmFullText.cfm<br />
?ID=20657&storytype=HerbalMon</p>

<p>Adverse Effects</p>

<p>The consequences of high doses or long-term use of licorice are<br />
severe. This herb can cause high blood pressure, low levels of<br />
potassium, fluid retention and swelling of the face and limbs,<br />
hormonal imbalance, and muscle destruction leading to pain and<br />
weakness.</p>

<p>At least one woman experienced loss of libido. Another woman ate<br />
too much licorice candy and lost a great deal of potassium; her<br />
heart stopped.</p>

<p>Licorice can also change heart rhythms, prolonging QT and PR<br />
intervals on an electrocardiogram.</p>

<p>Lethargy and fatigue as well as weakness are part of the picture of<br />
licorice toxicity.</p>

<p>Many of the negative symptoms associated with licorice are due to<br />
its ability to inhibit the renin-angiotensin system. Elderly people in<br />
particular are susceptible to kidney problems as a consequence of<br />
licorice.</p>

<p>Paralysis of the legs (and in one case, of all of the limbs) has been<br />
reported. A sixty-four-year-old man developed pulmonary edema,<br />
signaled by fatigue and trouble breathing, after eating four<br />
packages of black Twizzlers licorice candy in three days. This<br />
case demonstrates how quickly a serious reaction can arise.<br />
Licorice can reduce thyroid gland activity and lower the basal<br />
metabolic rate.</p>

<p>It appears that individuals vary considerably in their susceptibility to<br />
adverse reactions from licorice. Some people experience negative<br />
symptoms within days, while others may ingest excessive licorice<br />
in candy, chewing gum, chewing tobacco, or herbal medicine for<br />
months or even years before they realize that they are suffering<br />
damaging effects.</p>

<p>Women appear to be somewhat more susceptible than men, and<br />
oral contraceptives may increase this sensitivity.</p>

<p><hr><br />
From Karen<br />
</p>

	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001169.html">11:01 pm</a>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001314"></a>
<h3 class="title">sweet!  i didn't even know i had this paper.  thanks john!</h3>

<p>Structural Models for the Alkaline Conformers of Yeast iso-1-Ferricytochrome c</p>

<p><a href="http://www.sciencefromisrael.com/openurl.asp?genre=article&issn=0021-2148&volume=40&issue=1&spage=21"><br />
STEVEN R. NESS</a> A1, TERENCE P. LO A1, A. GRANT MAUK A1 </p>

<p>Israel Journal of Chemistry  <br />
   Publisher:   Laser Pages Publishing Ltd.  <br />
   Issue:   Volume 40, Number 1 / 2000  <br />
   Pages:   21 - 25  </p>

<p><br />
A1 Department of Biochemistry and Molecular Biology, University of British Columbia, Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada V6T 1Z3</p>

<p><br />
Abstract: </p>

<p>Structural models for three alkaline conformers of yeast iso-1- ferricytochrome c have been calculated from the atomic coordinates of the native protein through the use of molecular dynamics simulation. In the three models produced by this work, the Met80 axial ligand to the heme iron has been replaced by either Lys72, Lys73, or Lys79, and the related changes in structure of the cytochrome are described. The principal changes in cytochrome structure predicted to result from this pH-linked change in axial ligation involve location of residues 70 80, a region of the protein sequence that is phylogenetically conserved. The remainder of the protein fold in each model is essentially unchanged from the structure of the native protein, which is consistent with available spectroscopic information. The observation that this highly conserved region is apparently integrally involved in this conformational change may be interpreted as indicating a possible physiological role for the pH-linkage of ferricytochrome c structure. </p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001314.html">12:52 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1314" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<h2 class="date">juni 10, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001290"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p></p>

<p>a <a href="http://planetwaves.net/astrology/venustransit1.html">link</a></p>

<p>Aquarius (Jan. 20-Feb. 19)<br />
Healing always involves acknowledging pain or sickness on some level. As far as I can tell, affirming problems in clear terms is the best thing we can do in preparation for resolving them. In much the same way, we do tend to set up our lives such that pain is the most credible teacher. Are you ready for a new method of learning? I really hope so, because you are now being given one. But note this: to learn from creativity involves trading in the lessons of pain for another way of life. To learn from love involves gambling away the loneliness that has become so familiar. Is this really a risk? </p>

<p>thank you, srg.</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001290.html">10:38 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1290" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>

<h2 class="date">juni 06, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001277"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>Hear, O children of immortal bliss,<br />
You are born to be united with the Lord.<br />
Follow the path of the illumined ones<br />
And be united with the Lord of Life.</p>

<p>Kindle the fire of kundalini deep<br />
In meditation. Bring your mind and breath<br />
Under control. Drink deep of divine love,<br />
And you will attain the unitive state.</p>

<p>Dedicate yourself to the Lord of Life,<br />
Who is the cause of the cosmos. He will<br />
Remove the cause of all your suffering<br />
And free you from the bondage of karma.</p>

<p>-Shvetashvatara Upanishad<br />
Excerpted from The Upanishads, translated by Eknath Easwaran, copyright 1987. Reprinted with permission from Nilgiri Press,<br />
www.nilgiri.org.<br />
</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001277.html">09:12 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1277" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<h3 class="title">Printing Postscript files from .pdf files</h3>

<p>P.S. (ps is a directory)<br />
<pre><br />
acroread -toPostScript * ps<br />
</pre></p>

	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001262.html">10:37 am</a>

<h2 class="date">juli 13, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001336"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p><a href="http://www.thinkgeek.com/computing/drives/5ad4/"><img alt="pocketec.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/pocketec.jpg" width="228" height="172" border="0" /><br />
yum.</a></p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001336.html">08:37 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1336" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>





<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001335"></a>
<h3 class="title"><a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2004/07/13/science/13magn.html?pagewanted=2">nyt artickle</a></h3>

<p>Like many of the Earth's invisible rhythms, the field reversals are typically slow, taking anywhere from 5,000 to 7,000 years to complete.</p>

<p>Strong evidence of their reality first emerged in the 1950's and 1960's when scientists towing magnetic sensors behind ships found that the rocky seabed exhibited odd stripes of magnetization.</p>

<p>It turned out that continuous flows of seabed lava became alternately magnetized over the ages as the polarities of the Earth's field switched one way, then the other. The seabed acted like a huge tape recorder, and the same proved true of the layered deposits of old volcanoes on land.</p>

<p>How did the rocky memories form? Molten lava proved to hold tiny mineral grains that acted like innumerable compasses, or miniature magnets, freely aligning themselves with the contemporary field. But as the lava cooled, the tiny compasses froze in place, immobile even if the field shifted. Experts called it paleomagnetism and found that the tiny compasses were often made of magnetite, a naturally magnetic mineral.</p>

<p><img alt="sci_MAGNET_span.jpg" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/sci_MAGNET_span.jpg" width="583" height="212" border="0" /></p>

<p><br />
</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001335.html">05:39 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1335" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001326"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p><a href="http://www.psc.edu/~dnave/notes/w2kvmw.phtml">sweet</a> - instructions for getting vmware to run off a non-bootable cdrom.</p>

<pre>
You are here: www.psc.edu/ D. Nave @ psc.edu/ D. Nave's Notes/ Installing Win2K from CD in VM-Ware 3.2 for Linux 

<p>To install Windows 2000 Professional in VM-Ware 3.2 from non-bootable CD: <br />
Initialize a new VM-Ware config for Windows 2000 Professional via the configuration wizard. Point the CD-ROM device at its proper /dev location, but point the floppy at a file (e.g. /vmware/win2000Pro/floppy). VM-Ware will warn that this "device" doesn't exist. This is fine; continue anyway. Make sure the box is checked to enable (connect) the floppy at Power On. <br />
When the wizard is complete, select Settings -> Configuration Editor from VM-Ware's menu, and edit the Floppy Drives entry. Change the combo box from Device to File, and make sure that the path is the same as in (1). <br />
Mount your CD-ROM under Linux, and find cdboot1.img on the mounted file system. Copy cdboot1.img into the floppy's file (e.g. from (1) above). <br />
Power on VM-Ware. This should bring up the normal Windows 2000 Disk 1 installation screen. If not, make sure that: <br />
the Floppy configuration from Settings -> Configuration Editor points at the right file;<br />
that you've copied cdboot1.img into the file indicated below the combo box; and,<br />
that the floppy is connected at Power On (the corresponding check box should be darkened);<br />
When Windows 2000 Setup asks for a new Disk N, copy the corresponding cdbootN.img into the floppy file.<br />
That's it. Windows 2000 Setup should proceed as normal.<br />
Démian Nave @ PSC \\ Last updated 07:00pm 12/31/69, PHP V3.0.18</p>

<p></pre></p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001326.html">10:26 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1326" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>
	
	
</div>

<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001386.html">03:24 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1386" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (4)</a>
	
	
</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001385"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<pre>
set print elements number-of-elements 
</pre>
Set a limit on how many elements of an array GDB will print. If GDB is printing a large array, it stops printing after it has printed the number of elements set by the set print elements command. This limit also applies to the display of strings. Setting number-of-elements to zero means that the printing is unlimited.



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001385.html">10:35 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1385" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001383"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>If you get the following kind of error in gdb:</p>

<pre>
   1       ../sysdeps/i386/elf/start.S: No such file or directory.
           in ../sysdeps/i386/elf/start.S
</pre>

<p>Try setting your breakpoints or file commands with the full file name:</p>

<pre>
b file.c:1023
</pre>




<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001383.html">10:22 am</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1383" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>
	
	
</div>

<div class="posted">

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001372"></a>
<h3 class="title">displaying TLS axes</h3>

<pre>
tlsanl tlsin TLSOUT xyzin CRP-D53H2.pdb xyzout junk.pdb &lt;&lt; EOF |tee CRP-D53H2-TLS.html
bresid
AXES
end
EOF
awk '{if($1=="L"&&$2==2){getline;printf"%6.2f %6.2f %6.2f   ",$1,$2,$3;getline;printf"%6.2f %6.2f %6.2f %3d\n",$1,$2,$3,16+color}
else{if($1=="Q"){color+=4} else{if($1=="!"){printf"# %s\n",$0}}}}' AXES &gt; TLS_AXES.vu
</pre>                                        




<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001372.html">12:21 pm</a>
		| <a href="http://www.sness.net/cgi-bin/nmt/mt-comments.cgi?entry_id=1372" onclick="OpenComments(this.href); return false">Comments (1)</a>

<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001418"></a>
<h3 class="title">pdbset</h3>

<p>to convert a pdb file into a .pir file with the standard one letter sequence:</p>

<pre>
pdbset XYZIN $1.pdb XYZOUT coords/$1_out.pdb << END > log/$1.log
EXCLUDE HOH
SEQUENCE SINGLE $1.pir
END
</pre>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001418.html">09:03 am</a>
	
	
</div>

<h2 class="date">oktober 22, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001414"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>nethack patch ideas:</p>

<p>if you polymorph into a troll, you discover you were just "mostly dead" and<br />
not "all dead", and become alive again.</p>

<p>if you are a two-headed troll, you can wear two amulets.</p>

<p>trolls can wear amulets of life-saving</p>

<p>if a human is around, and if there is water around, and if you are polymorphed<br />
into a troll, the human will try to pick you up and throw you in the water, killing you permanently, just like a troll.</p>

<p><br />
Miracle Max : He probably owes you money huh? I'll ask him. <br />
Inigo Montoya : He's dead. He can't talk. <br />
Miracle Max : Whoo-hoo-hoo, look who knows so much. It just so happens that your friend here is only MOSTLY dead. There's a big difference between mostly dead and all dead. Mostly dead is slightly alive. With all dead, well, with all dead there's usually only one thing you can do. <br />
Inigo Montoya : What's that? <br />
Miracle Max : Go through his clothes and look for loose change. <br />
</p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001414.html">12:09 am</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>



<h2 class="date">oktober 21, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001413"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>google news should totally have a ROT-13 detector for groups like<br />
rec.games.roguelike.nethack.  a small but nice tweak.  you could look<br />
for letter frequency or something, and it would be just a few groups<br />
that actually still use ROT-13 that it would be useful for.</p>

<p>i see it as</p>

<p>rot-13 detected - click here to show<br />
<pre><br />
> "Lbh unir uvqqra tbyq."--Zber--<br />
> "Zbfg yvxryl nyy lbhe tbyq jnf fgbyra sebz guvf inhyg."--Zber--<br />
> "Cyrnfr qebc gung tbyq naq sbyybj zr."<br />
</pre></p>

<p>changing to </p>

<p>rot 13 detected - click here to hide<br />
<pre><br />
"Lbh unir uvqqra tbyq."--Zber--<br />
"Zbfg yvxryl nyy lbhe tbyq jnf fgbyra sebz guvf inhyg."--Zber--<br />
"Cyrnfr qebc gung tbyq naq sbyybj zr."<br />
</pre><br />
rot 13<br />
<pre><br />
"You have hidden gold."--More--<br />
"Most likely all your gold was stolen from this vault."--More--<br />
"Please drop that gold and follow me."<br />
</pre></p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001413.html">11:43 pm</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>

<h2 class="date">November 05, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001429"></a>
<h3 class="title"></h3>

<p>lrm Low wavelength remote - f' small, f'' large<br />
peak Peak of absorption - f' large, f'' very large<br />
infl Point of inflection - f' very large, f'' small<br />
hrm High wavelength remote - f' small, f'' very small</p>

<p><img alt="crossec.gif" src="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/crossec.gif" width="429" height="326" border="0" /></p>

<p>also, a nice <a href="http://www.bmsc.washington.edu/scatter/AS_form.html">website</a> to calculate the f' (fprime) and f'' (fdoubleprime) terms from the element.  From Ethan Merritt. </p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001429.html">03:59 PM</a>
	
	
</div>

<h2 class="date">November 02, 2004</h2>


<div class="blogbody">
<a name="001426"></a>
<h3 class="title">tcl scripting quoting substitution</h3>

<p>I found this syntax summary on the web in March 2001, but couldn't find it again now: ( in 2002, this summary has been added in the wiki: An Introduction to Tcl Scripting)<br />
<pre><br />
Script = commands separated by newlines or semicolons. <br />
Command = words separated by white space. <br />
$ causes variable substitution. <br />
[] causes command substitution. <br />
"" quotes white space and semi-colons. <br />
{} quotes all special characters. <br />
\ quotes next character, provides C-like substitution. <br />
# for comments (must be at beginning of command).<br />
</pre></p>



<div class="posted">
	Posted by sness at <a href="http://www.sness.net/weblog/archives/001426.html">11:01 AM</a>
	
	
</div>

</div>
